        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered attractive alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for next-generation sustainable and large-scale electrochem. energy storage.  Org. sodium-ion batteries (OSIBs) using environmentally benign org. materials as electrodes, which demonstrate high energy/power d. and good structural designability, have recently attracted great attention.  Nevertheless, the practical applications and popularization of OSIBs are generally restricted by the intrinsic disadvantages related to org. electrodes, such as their low cond., poor stability, and high soly. in electrolytes.  Here, the latest research progress with regard to electrode materials of OSIBs, ranging from small mols. to org. polymers, is systematically reviewed, with the main focus on the mol. structure design/modification, the electrochem. behavior, and the corresponding charge-storage mechanism.  Particularly, the challenges faced by OSIBs and the effective design strategies are comprehensively summarized from three aspects: function-oriented mol. design, micromorphol. regulation, and construction of org.-inorg. composites.  Finally, the perspectives and opportunities in the research of org. electrode materials are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxZtUKbEdsT7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgChL8vqda5Sw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1Grtrw%253D&amp;md5=e8f2c8e2e5398d80860a7d9330a42440</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202001440"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fast Rate and Long Life Potassium-Ion Based Dual-Ion Battery through 3D Porous Organic Negative Electrode</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fast Rate and Long Life Potassium-Ion Based Dual-Ion Battery through 3D Porous Organic Negative Electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Ao; Pan, Qingguang; Zhang, Miao; Xie, Donghao; Tang, Yongbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-based dual ion batteries (K-DIBs) with potassium cation (K+) intercalation graphitic anodes have been investigated for their potential in large-scale energy storage applications owing to their merits of low cost and environmental friendly.  Nonetheless, graphite anodes are plagued by vol. expansion from the large K+ ions and the co-intercalation of solvent mols. during the charging.  Accordingly, org. materials stand out for the flexible adjustable structures and abundant active sites, which can accommodate cations by multiple functional groups without structural collapse.  However, K-DIBs based on org. anodes have rarely been investigated.  Herein, 3D porous dipotassium terephthalate nanosheets are synthesized via a freeze-dry method as the K-DIB anode, which can reversibly store K+ ions at a fast rate with a high specific capacity and robust stability due to the sufficient redox active sites and diffusion pathways of K+ ions in the 3D porous structure.  Consequently, a novel K-DIB configuration combining this fast kinetics org. anode and environmental friendly expanded graphite (EG) cathode is constructed (pK2TP//EG), which exhibits a high specific capacity (68 mAh g-1 at 2 C), good rate performance up to 20 C, and long cycling life with a capacity retention ~ 100% after 2000 cycles, which is the best performance obsd. among reported K-DIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIqQuN6IjGOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0MtU6hW45nA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXosF2qsbk%253D&amp;md5=34e7c5e58e6f6485b21d83faea6b33b5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/admi.201700059"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Khan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Senthilkumar, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shanker, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ko, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Redox-Additive-Enhanced High Capacitance Supercapacitors Based on Co<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> Nanosheets</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of a water oxidn. catalyst has been a demanding challenge in realizing water splitting systems.  The asym. geometry and flexible ligation of the biol. Mn4CaO5 cluster are important properties for the function of photosystem II, and these properties can be applied to the design of new inorg. water oxidn. catalysts.  We identified a new crystal structure, Mn3(PO4)2·3H2O, that ppts. spontaneously in aq. soln. at room temp. and demonstrated its high catalytic performance under neutral conditions.  The bulky phosphate polyhedron induces a less-ordered Mn geometry in Mn3(PO4)2·3H2O.  Computational anal. indicated that the structural flexibility in Mn3(PO4)2·3H2O could stabilize the Jahn-Teller-distorted Mn(III) and thus facilitate Mn(II) oxidn.  This study provides valuable insights into the interplay between at. structure and catalytic activity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoZm5nlieW3zLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0MtU6hW45nA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmslSqs7o%253D&amp;md5=5c9721f09a78087e9eeb8cfbd64a87fc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201801984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Interlayer-Spacing-Regulated VOPO<sub>4</sub> Nanosheets with Fast Kinetics for High-Capacity and Durable Rechargeable Magnesium Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An advanced high-energy sodium ion full battery based on nanostructured Na2Ti3O7/VOPO4 layered materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hongsen; Peng, Lele; Zhu, Yue; Chen, Dahong; Zhang, Xiaogang; Yu, Guihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In virtue of the abundant sodium resources, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered to be one of the promising alternatives to lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, current research concs. mostly on sodium ion half-cells, and the development of sodium ion full cells with high performance remains a crit. challenge.  Here we rationally designed a full sodium-ion battery based on nanostructured Na2Ti3O7 and VOPO4 materials as the anodes and cathodes, owing to their advantageous electrochem. features.  The full cell outputs one of the highest operating voltages close to 2.9 V and delivers a large reversible capacity of 114 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.1C.  It also shows outstanding rate capability (∼74 mA h g-1 at 2C rate) and excellent cycling stability (92.4% capacity retention after 100 cycles).  A high energy d. of 220 W h kg-1 is achieved, which is comparable to the state-of-the-art LIBs.  Moreover, the temp.-dependent charge-discharge tests indicate excellent capacity retentions in a wide temp. range of -20 to 55 °C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoeiSHi_Z7ig7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0MtU6hW45nA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVCmsb7J&amp;md5=e38751b094eee46fa6320e8370c3026b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1016/0025-5408(85)90023-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">de

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Isotypic Na7(MP2O7)4PO4 (I; M = Al, Cr, Fe) (tetragonal, space group P‾421c) were prepd.  The structure of I (M = Fe) was solved and refined to a final R = 0.037 for 577 independent reflections.  It consists of (FeP2O7)4PO4 units interconnected so as to form a 3-dimensional framework into which the Na ions are inserted.  The units are made of a PO4 tetrahedron linked to 4 FeO6 octahedra; each octahedron is connected to a P2O7 group by 2 O atoms.  Ion exchange expts. and cond. measurements give evidence of some mobility of the Na ions at high temp.  However, the σ-values (∼10-5Ω-1cm-1 at 300°) are relatively low.  The narrowness of the windows between the Na sites as well as the presence of an O atom linked to only 1 polyhedron of the framework are unfavorable features to fast cation transport.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpIcT6SGA4zprVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljU0rmGsVuQTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaL2MXhslyjsbo%253D&amp;md5=f56a0699c993188fab348b47056153d5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201200920"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahn, H.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Toward a Reversible Mn4+/Mn2+ Redox Reaction and Dendrite-Free Zn Anode in Near-Neutral Aqueous Zn/MnO2 Batteries via Salt Anion Chemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zeng, Xiaohui; Liu, Jiatu; Mao, Jianfeng; Hao, Junnan; Wang, Zhijie; Zhou, Si; Ling, Chris D.; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">32</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable aq. Zn/MnO2 batteries are very attractive large-scale energy storage technologies, but still suffer from limited cycle life and low capacity.  Here the novel adoption of a near-neutral acetate-based electrolyte (pH ≈ 6) is presented to promote the two-electron Mn4+/Mn2+ redox reaction and simultaneously enable a stable Zn anode.  The acetate anion triggers a highly reversible MnO2/Mn2+ reaction, which ensures high capacity and avoids the issue of structural collapse of MnO2.  Meanwhile, the anode-friendly electrolyte enables a dendrite-free Zn anode with outstanding stability and high plating/stripping Coulombic efficiency (99.8%).  Hence, a high capacity of 556 mA h g-1, a lifetime of 4000 cycles without decay, and excellent rate capability up to 70 mA cm-2 are demonstated in this new near-neutral aq. Zn/MnO2 battery by simply manipulating the salt anion in the electrolyte.  The acetate anion not only modifies the surface properties of MnO2 cathode but also creates a highly compatible environment for the Zn anode.  This work provides a new opportunity for developing high-performance Zn/MnO2 and other aq. batteries based on the salt anion chem.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpemFwJ0VV7rrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljU0rmGsVuQTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlShu7nF&amp;md5=9a134ba39d67a5689251509d236fbe5e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.01.009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tuning Nitrogen Species in Three-Dimensional Porous Carbon via Phosphorus Doping for Ultra-Fast Potassium Storage</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>57</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">728</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">736</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tuning nitrogen species in three-dimensional porous carbon via phosphorus doping for ultra-fast potassium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Hanna; Huang, Dan; Tang, Yougen; Wang, Qi; Ji, Xiaobo; Wang, Haiyan; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">57</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbonaceous materials have been proved to be promising materials for energy storage.  Heteroatom doping, esp. N doping, could further promote their electrochem. performance, and the type of doped N configuration plays a key role in detg. the reactivity of doped carbon.  However, achieving a high proportion of active N (pyridinic N) in N doped carbon is still a big challenge.  In this work, we successfully tuned the N species and achieved high-level pyridinic N in carbon via constructing a three-dimensional (3D) honeycomb-like structure in conjunction with phosphorus doping.  The 3D porous structure with sufficient pore defects and edges provides the preconditions for the formation of pyridinic N, and the subsequent P-doping leads to more open edge sites, which further facilitate the formation of pyridinic N.  This modification greatly promoted the reactivity of the carbon framework, contributing to rapid interfacial K+ adsorption reactions.  The as-obtained P-doped N-rich honeycomb-like carbon thus achieved ultrahigh reversible capacity and outstanding rate capability (with capacities of 419.3 and 270.4 mA h g-1 obtained at 100 and 1000 mA g-1, resp.).  This outstanding performance demonstrates that adjusting the proportion of active N in N-doped carbon offers a promising approach toward excellent N-doped carbon materials for energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq_CiqurnzYX7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljU0rmGsVuQTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXpvF2hsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=de75b88e54948e907121aad2e9d29e4a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201803210"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">There exists a strong demand to replace expensive noble metal catalysts with cheap metal sulfides or phosphides for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER).  Recently metal phosphides such as NixP, FeP and CoP have been considered as promising candidates to replace Pt cathodes.  Here we report that the nanocryst. CoP nanosheet assembly on carbon cloth can be formed by a two-step process: electrochem. deposition of Co species followed by gas phase phosphidation.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Core-Shell ZIF-8@ZIF-67-Derived CoP Nanoparticle-Embedded N-Doped Carbon Nanotube Hollow Polyhedron for Efficient Overall Water Splitting</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Yuan; Sun, Kaian; Liu, Shoujie; Cao, Xing; Wu, Konglin; Cheong, Weng-Chon; Chen, Zheng; Wang, Yu; Li, Yang; Liu, Yunqi; Wang, Dingsheng; Peng, Qing; Chen, Chen; Li, Yadong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">140</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2610-2618</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The construction of highly active and stable non-noble-metal electrocatalysts for hydrogen and oxygen evolution reactions is a major challenge for overall water splitting.  Herein, we report a novel hybrid nanostructure with CoP nanoparticles (NPs) embedded in a N-doped carbon nanotube hollow polyhedron (NCNHP) through a pyrolysis-oxidn.-phosphidation strategy derived from core-shell ZIF-8@ZIF-67.  Benefiting from the synergistic effects between highly active CoP NPs and NCNHP, the CoP/NCNHP hybrid exhibited outstanding bifunctional electrocatalytic performances.  When the CoP/NCNHP was employed as both the anode and cathode for overall water splitting, a potential as low as 1.64 V was needed to achieve the c.d. of 10 mA·cm-2, and it still exhibited superior activity after continuously working for 36 h with nearly negligible decay in potential.  D. functional theory calcns. indicated that the electron transfer from NCNHP to CoP could increase the electronic states of the Co d-orbital around the Fermi level, which could increase the binding strength with H and therefore improve the electrocatalytic performance.  The strong stability is attributed to high oxidn. resistance of the CoP surface protected by the NCNHP.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLz4Hvdf-8jbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgi5wWt77KZFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1Gns74%253D&amp;md5=5d958f8cd25a4961f74b92810f753e1e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201801013"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Plasma-Induced Amorphous Shell and Deep Cation-Site S Doping Endow TiO<sub>2</sub> with Extraordinary Sodium Storage Performance</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure-dependent performance of TiO2/C as anode material for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Hanna; Gan, Qingmeng; Wang, Haiyan; Xu, Gui-Liang; Zhang, Xiaoyi; Huang, Dan; Fu, Fang; Tang, Yougen; Amine, Khalil; Shao, Minhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">217-227</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The performance of energy storage materials is highly dependent on their nanostructures.  Herein, hierarchical rod-in-tube TiO2 with a uniform carbon coating is synthesized as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries by a facile solvothermal method.  This unique structure consists of a tunable nanorod core, interstitial hollow spaces, and a functional nanotube shell assembled from two-dimensional nanosheets.  By adjusting the types of solvents used and reaction time, the morphologies of TiO2/C composites can be tuned to nanoparticles, microrods, rod-in-tube structures, or microtubes.  Among these materials, rod-in-tube TiO2 with a uniform carbon coating shows the highest electronic cond., sp. surface area (336.4 m2 g-1), and porosity, and these factors lead to the best sodium storage capability.  Benefiting from the unique structural features and improved electronic/ionic cond., the as-obtained rod-in-tube TiO2/C in coin cell tests exhibits a high discharge capacity of 277.5 and 153.9 mAh g-1 at 50 and 5000 mA g-1, resp., and almost 100% capacity retention over 14,000 cycles at 5000 mA g-1.  In operando high-energy X-ray diffraction further confirms the stable crystal structure of the rod-in-tube TiO2/C during Na+ insertion/extn.  This work highlights that nanostructure design is an effective strategy to achieve advanced energy storage materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqe-RMEbotlg7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgi5wWt77KZFA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">1T MoS2 nanosheets with extraordinary sodium storage properties via thermal-driven ion intercalation assisted exfoliation of bulky MoS2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Dan; Huang, Dan; Wang, Haiyan; Xu, Gui-Liang; Zhang, Xiaoyi; Zhang, Rui; Tang, Yougen; Abd Ei-Hady, Deia; Alshitari, Wael; Saad Al-Bogami, Abdullah; Amine, Khalil; Shao, Minhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">61</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">361-369</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic phase (1T) MoS2 has attracted enormous attention as an appealing energy storage material for batteries, supercapacitors, and catalysts.  However, a facile fabrication method is lacking and the intensive understanding of its sodium storage mechanism is absent.  Herein, ultrathin 1T MoS2 nanosheets (1-2 layers) are directly fabricated via and are investigated as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  Interestingly, the as-prepd. 1T MoS2 nanosheets demonstrate a high reversible capacity of 450 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and outstanding cycling stability with a high capacity retention ratio of 94% after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1, which is far superior to that of the 2H phase counterpart.  D. function theory (DFT) calcns. show that, in addn. to significantly enhanced electronic cond., 1T MoS2 also possesses much more sodium philicity and faster Na atom mobility in comparison with the 2H phase.  More importantly, as revealed by ex-situ Raman, in-situ X-ray diffraction, and DFT calcns., the 1T MoS2 is more capable of suppressing the dissoln. of S species from the material structure compared with the 2H phase, leading to excellent cycling stability.  The facile and easily scalable method as well as the deep mechanism anal. will provide a very important ref. for the development of high-performance MoS2 anodes and other SIB electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDiFZSfYOmXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgqKZTAY_l3Xw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXovVyiu70%253D&amp;md5=b451d90d35b6481b1cffaebdafc4d3fd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201903826"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Long, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1903826</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201903826</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D1903826%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DF.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BHong%26author%3DJ.%2BHao%26author%3DS.%2BZhang%26author%3DG.%2BLiang%26author%3DJ.%2BLong%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DN.%2BLiu%26author%3DW.%2BK.%2BPang%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DUltrathin%2BFew-Layer%2BGeP%2BNanosheets%2Bvia%2BLithiation-Assisted%2BChemical%2BExfoliation%2Band%2BTheir%2BApplication%2Bin%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201903826&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c08950&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201903826&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin Few-Layer GeP Nanosheets via Lithiation-Assisted Chemical Exfoliation and Their Application in Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Fuhua; Hong, Jian; Hao, Junnan; Zhang, Shilin; Liang, Gemeng; Long, Jun; Liu, Yuqing; Liu, Nana; Pang, Wei Kong; Chen, Jun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1903826</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultrathin few-layer materials have attracted intensive research attention because of their distinctive and unique properties.  Few-layer GeP (FL-GP) is potentially interesting for application in electronics and optoelectronics because of its appropriate band gap and good stability under ambient conditions.  Nevertheless, it is a challenge to achieve ultrathin few-layer or single layer GeP from exfoliation of bulk crystals.  Here, a lithiation-assisted chem. exfoliation technique is employed to achieve FL-GP, in which the interlayer spacing can be efficiently enlarged after a preliminary lithium ion intercalation, allowing the bulk crystal to be readily exfoliated in a following ultrasonication.  As a result, ultrathin FL-GP is obtained.  In a demonstration, the FL-GP/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) demonstrates remarkable sodium storage performance.  The FL-GP with a two-dimensional structure shortens the ion transport pathways and alleviates the vol. variation during sodiation.  Meanwhile, the rGO in the composite improves the cond. of the whole electrode.  The as-prepd. FL-GP/rGO electrode exhibits a high capacity of 504.2 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, remarkable rate performance, and superior cycling stability in the half cells.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Half-Cell and Full-Cell Applications of Highly Stable and Binder-Free Sodium Ion Batteries Based on Cu3P Nanowire Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Mouping; Chen, Yu; Xie, Yihao; Yang, Tingzhou; Shen, Xiaowei; Xu, Na; Yu, Haiying; Yan, Chenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion battery (SIB) is esp. attractive in cost-effective energy storage device as an alternative to lithium-ion battery.  Particularly, metal phosphides as potential anodes for SIBs have recently been demonstrated owing to their higher specific capacities compared with those of carbonaceous materials.  Unfortunately, most reported metal phosphides consist of irregular particles ranged from several hundreds nanometers to tens of micrometers, thus delivering limited cyclic stability.  This paper reports the sodium storage properties of additive-free Cu3P nanowire (CPNW) anode directly grown on copper current collector via an in situ growth followed by phosphidation method.  Therefore, as a result of its structure features, CPNW anode demonstrates highly stable cycling ability with an ≈70% retention in capacity at the 260th cycle, whereas most reported metal phosphides have limited cycle nos. ranged between 30 and 150.  Besides, the reaction mechanism between Cu3P and Na is investigated by examg. the intermediate products at different charge/discharge stages using ex situ X-ray diffraction measurements.  Furthermore, to explore the practical application of CPNW anode, a pouch-type Na+ full cell consisting of CPNW anode and Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode is assembled and characterized.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering that the high capacity, long-term cycle life, and high-rate capability of anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is a bottleneck currently, a series of Co-doped FeS2 solid solns. with different Co contents were prepd. by a facile solvothermal method, and for the first time their Na-storage properties were investigated.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Defect-rich TiO2-δ nanocrystals confined in a mooncake-shaped porous carbon matrix as an advanced Na ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Hanna; Zhang, Qi; Wang, Haiyan; Zhang, Hehe; Li, Jiadong; Peng, Zhiguang; Tang, Yougen; Shao, Minhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Inferior electronic cond. and sluggish sodium ion diffusion are still two big challenges for TiO2 anode material for Na ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, we synthesize TiO2/C composites by the pyrolysis of MIL-125(Ti) precursor and successfully introduce defects to TiO2/C composite by a simple magnesium redn.  The as-prepd. defect-rich TiO2-δ/C composite shows mooncake-shaped morphol. consisting of TiO2-δ nanocrystals with an av. particle size of 5 nm well dispersed in the carbon matrix.  When used as a SIBs anode, the defect-rich TiO2-δ/C composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 330.2 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 at the voltage range of 0.001-3.0 V and long-term cycling stability with negligible decay after 5000 cycles.  Compared with other four TiO2/C samples, the electrochem. performance of defect-rich TiO2-δ/C is highly improved, which may benefit from the enhanced electronic/ionic conductivities owing to the defect-rich features, high surface area rendering shortened electronic and ionic diffusion path, and the suppress of the TiO2 crystal aggregation during sodiation and desodiation process by the carbon matrix.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGro_u8mtEdwubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgqKZTAY_l3Xw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering Textile Electrode and Bacterial Cellulose Nanofiber Reinforced Hydrogel Electrolyte to Enable High-Performance Flexible All-Solid-State Supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xiaolong; Yuan, Libei; Liu, Rong; He, Hanna; Hao, Junnan; Lu, Yan; Wang, Yuanming; Liang, Gemeng; Yuan, Guohui; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The fabrication of highly durable, flexible, all-solid-state supercapacitors (ASCs) remains challenging because of the unavoidable mech. stress that such devices are subjected to in wearable applications.  Natural/artificial fiber textiles are regarded as prospective materials for flexible ASCs due to their outstanding physicochem. properties.  Here, a high-performance ASC is designed by employing graphene-encapsulated polyester fiber loaded with polyaniline as the flexible electrodes and bacterial cellulose (BC) nanofiber-reinforced polyacrylamide as the hydrogel electrolyte.  The ASC combines the textile electrode capable of arbitrary deformation with the BC-reinforced hydrogel with high ionic cond. (125 mS cm-1), high tensile strength (330 kPa), and superelasticity (stretchability up to ≈1300%), giving rise to a device with high stability/compatibility between the electrodes and electrolyte that is compliant with flexible electronics.  As a result, this ASC delivers high areal capacitance of 564 mF cm-2, excellent rate capability, good energy/power densities, and more importantly, superior mech. properties without significant capacitance degrdn. after repeated bending, confirming the functionality of the ASC under mech. deformation.  This work demonstrates an effective design for a sufficiently tough energy storage device, which shows great potential in truly wearable applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpCw5laytcWM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY1IndIwxpLA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon Electrodes for K-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jian, Zelang; Luo, Wei; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors for the 1st time report electrochem. K insertion in graphite in a nonaq. electrolyte, which can exhibit a high reversible capacity of 273 mA h/g.  Ex situ XRD studies confirm that KC36, KC24, and KC8 sequentially form upon potassiation, whereas depotassiation recovers graphite through phase transformations in an opposite sequence.  Graphite shows moderate rate capability and relatively fast capacity fading.  To improve the performance of C K-ion anodes, the authors synthesized a non-graphitic soft C that exhibits cyclability and rate capability much superior to that of graphite.  This work may open up a new paradigm toward rechargeable K-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqn7rXCBe-h7bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY1IndIwxpLA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVCgu7%252FK&amp;md5=1a60438c51bd3792cb2827cee8239099</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501874"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jian, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bommier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard Carbon Microspheres: Potassium-Ion Anode <i>versus</i> Sodium-Ion Anode</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.08.002</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D40%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D1-8%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DP.%2BLian%26author%3DY.%2BDong%26author%3DZ.-S.%2BWu%26author%3DS.%2BZheng%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DS.%2BWang%26author%3DC.%2BSun%26author%3DJ.%2BQin%26author%3DX.%2BShi%26author%3DX.%2BBao%26title%3DAlkalized%2BTi3C2%2BMXene%2BNanoribbons%2Bwith%2BExpanded%2BInterlayer%2BSpacing%2Bfor%2BHigh-Capacity%2BSodium%2Band%2BPotassium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2017.08.002&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c08950&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2017.08.002&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Alkalized Ti3C2 MXene nanoribbons with expanded interlayer spacing for high-capacity sodium and potassium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lian, Peichao; Dong, Yanfeng; Wu, Zhong-Shuai; Zheng, Shuanghao; Wang, Xiaohui; Sen Wang; Sun, Chenglin; Qin, Jieqiong; Shi, Xiaoyu; Bao, Xinhe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">40</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1-8</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As post-lithium ion batteries, both sodium ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium ion batteries (PIBs) possess great potential for large scale energy storage.  However, the improvements of both SIBs and PIBs for practical applications are facing great challenges in the development of high-performance electrode materials.  Here, we demonstrate the fabrication of alkalized Ti3C2 (a-Ti3C2) MXene nanoribbons attained by continuous shaking treatment of pristine Ti3C2 MXene in aq. KOH soln.  Benefited from the expanded interlayer spacing of a-Ti3C2, narrow widths of nanoribbons as well as three-dimensional interconnected porous frameworks for enhanced ion reaction kinetics and improved structure stability, the resulting a-Ti3C2 anodes showed excellent sodium/potassium storage performance, for example, high reversible capacities of 168 and 136 mA h g-1 at 20 mA g-1 and 84 and 78 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 were obtained for SIBs and PIBs, resp.  Notably, a-Ti3C2 possessed outstanding long-term cyclability at high c.d. of 200 mA g-1, delivering a capacity of ∼ 50 mA h g-1 for SIBs and ∼ 42 mA h g-1 for PIBs after 500 cycles, which outperformed most of reported MXene based anodes for SIBs and PIBs.  Moreover, this alkalization strategy could be extended as a universal approach for fabricating various alkalized MXene-based frameworks derived from a large family of MAX phases for numerous applications, such as catalysis, energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGolT0tcMvFiOLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY1IndIwxpLA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtlaku7zP&amp;md5=66f3d7c437c07405ca11840e3c6cc812</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.6b12185"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphorus-Based Alloy Materials for Advanced Potassium-Ion Battery Anode</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>139</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3316</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3319</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacs.6b12185</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D139%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D3316-3319%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BMao%26author%3DS.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BChen%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DPhosphorus-Based%2BAlloy%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BAdvanced%2BPotassium-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnode%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fjacs.6b12185&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c08950&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fjacs.6b12185&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-Based Alloy Materials for Advanced Potassium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenchao; Mao, Jianfeng; Li, Sean; Chen, Zhixin; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">139</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3316-3319</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) are interesting as one of the alternative metal-ion battery systems to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to the abundance and low cost of potassium.  The Sn4P3/C composite is investigated as a novel anode material for PIBs.  The electrode delivered a reversible capacity of 384.8 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and a good rate capability of 221.9 mA h g-1, even at 1 A g-1.  Its electrochem. performance is better than any anode material reported so far for PIBs.  It was also found that the Sn4P3/C electrode displays a discharge potential plateau of 0.1 V in PIBs, slightly higher than for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) (0.01 V), and well above the plating potential of metal.  This diminishes the formation of dendrites during cycling, and thus Sn4P3 is a relatively safe anode material, esp. for application in large-scale energy storage, where large amts. of electrode materials are used.  Furthermore, a possible reaction mechanism of the Sn4P3/C composite as PIB anode is proposed.  This work may open up a new avenue for further development of alloy-based anodes with high capacity and long cycle life for PIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqOqmqNddh2PbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY1IndIwxpLA"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjMUNONnlShg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvF2rsbk%253D&amp;md5=cfc7b2d153696dcbded22d954ff06174</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201904320"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium/Potassium-Ion Batteries: Boosting The Rate Capability and Cycle Life by Combining Morphology, Defect and Structure Engineering</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1904320</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium/Potassium-Ion Batteries: Boosting the Rate Capability and Cycle Life by Combining Morphology, Defect and Structure Engineering</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Huijuan; Xu, Rui; Feng, Yuezhan; Zeng, Sifan; Jiang, Yu; Wang, Huijuan; Luo, Wei; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-based materials have been considered as the most promising anode materials for both sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs), owing to their good chem. stability, high elec. cond., and environmental benignity.  However, due to the large sizes of sodium and potassium ions, it is a great challenge to realize a carbon anode with high reversible capacity, long cycle life, and high rate capability.  Herein, by rational design, N-doped 3D mesoporous carbon nanosheets (N-CNS) are successfully synthesized, which can realize unprecedented electrochem. performance for both SIBs and PIBs.  The N-CNS possess an ultrathin nanosheet structure with hierarchical pores, ultrahigh level of pyridinic N/pyrrolic N, and an expanded interlayer distance.  The beneficial features that can enhance the Na-/K-ion intercalation/deintercalation kinetic process, shorten the diffusion length for both ions and electrons, and accommodate the vol. change are demonstrated.  Hence, the N-CNS-based electrode delivers a high capacity of 239 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 10 000 cycles for SIBs and 321 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 5000 cycles for PIBs.  First-principles calcn. shows that the ultrahigh doping level of pyridinic N/pyrrolic N contributes to the enhanced sodium and potassium storage performance by modulating the charge d. distribution on the carbon surface.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpVG-cQvHto_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjMUNONnlShg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXpt12kuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=03d6ec4c0f67558dd6c91962115a7d5f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/sus2.4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, H.                 10.1002/sus2.4</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A perspective on sustainable energy materials for lithium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Xin-Bing; Liu, He; Yuan, Hong; Peng, Hong-Jie; Tang, Cheng; Huang, Jia-Qi; Zhang, Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">SusMat</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">38-50</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SUSMBP</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2692-4552</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium ion battery has achieved great success in portable electronics and even recently electronic vehicles since its commercialization in 1990s.  However, lithium-ion batteries are confronted with several issues in terms of the sustainable development such as the high price of raw materials and electronic products, the emerging safety accidents, etc.  The recent progresses are herein emphasized on lithium batteries for energy storage to clearly understand the sustainable energy chem. and emerging energy materials.  The Perspective presents novel lithium-ion batteries developed with the aims of enhancing the electrochem. performance and sustainability of energy storage systems.  First, revolutionary material chemistries, including novel low-cobalt cathode, org. electrode, and aq. electrolyte, are discussed.  Then, the characteristics of safety performance are analyzed and strategies to enhance safety are subsequently evaluated.  Battery recycling is considered as the key factor for a sustainable society and related technologies are present as well.  Finally, conclusion and outlook are drawn to shed lights on the further development of sustainable lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqi-VUKeoyALVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhjMUNONnlShg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXivFGis7c%253D&amp;md5=5e9381afd15f9f89e00b8a074fe86aed</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201903194"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mi, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress on The Alloy-Based Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries and Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1903194</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.201903194</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent progress on alloy-based anode for sodium-ion batteries and potassium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Keming; Liu, Chuntai; Mi, Liwei; Chou, Shulei; Chen, Weihua; Shen, Changyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1903194</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  High-energy batteries with low cost are urgently needed in the field of large-scale energy storage, such as grid systems and renewable energy sources.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) with alloy-based anodes provide huge potential due to their earth abundance, high capacity, and suitable working potential, and are recognized as attractive alternatives for next-generation batteries system.  Although some important breakthroughs have been reported, more significant improvements are still required for long lifetime and high energy d.  Herein, the latest progress for alloy-based anodes for SIBs and PIBs is summarized, mainly including Sn, Sb, Ge, Bi, Si, P, and their oxides, sulfides, selenides, and phosphides.  Specifically, the material designs for the desired Na+/K+ storage performance, phase transform, ionic/electronic transport kinetics, and specific chem. interactions are discussed.  Typical structural features and research strategies of alloy-based anodes, which are used to facilitate processes in battery development for SIBs and PIBs, are also summarized.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The practical application of germanium phosphide (GeP) in battery systems is seriously impeded referring to the sluggish reaction kinetics and severe vol. change.  Nanostructure design that elaborately resolves the above issues is highly desired but still remains a big challenge.  Herein, unique hollow nanoreactors assembled with nitrogen-doped carbon networks for in situ synthesis of the GeP electrodes are proposed for the first time.  Such nanoreactors form a self-supported conductive network, ensuring sufficient electrolyte infiltration and fast electron transport.  They restrain crystal growth and accommodate the vol. expansion of GeP simultaneously.  Reaction kinetics and confinement effect are optimized through nanoreactor size regulation.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Vacancy engineering is a promising approach for optimizing the energy storage performance of transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) due to the unique properties of vacancies in manipulating the electronic structure and active sites.  Nevertheless, achieving effective introduction of anion vacancies with adjustable vacancy concn. on a large scale is still a big challenge.  Herein, MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloys with anion vacancies introduced in situ have been achieved by a simple alloying reaction, and the vacancy concn. has been optimized through adjusting the chem. compn.  Exptl. and d. functional theory calcn. results suggest that the anion vacancies in MoS2(1-x)Se2x alloys could enhance the electronic cond., induce more active sites, and alleviate structural variation in the alloys during the potassium storage process.  When applied as potassium ion battery anodes, the most optimized vacancy-rich MoSSe alloy delivered high reversible capacities of 517.4 and 362.4 mAh g-1 at 100 and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  Moreover, a reversible capacity of 220.5 mAh g-1 could be maintained at 2000 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles.  This work demonstrates a practical approach to modifying the electronic and defect properties of TMDs, providing an effective strategy for constructing advanced electrode materials for battery systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXdcW5odM6NLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHAcHioOPm4g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvVantrbK&amp;md5=bdf190a3483499180c6f2375a012a109</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202001265"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The design and construction of flexible electrodes that can function at high rates and high areal capacities are essential regarding the practical application of flexible sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and other energy storage devices, which remains significantly challenging by far.  Herein, a flexible and 3D porous graphene nanosheet/SnS2 (3D-GNS/SnS2) film is reported as a high-performance SIB electrode.  In this hybrid film, the GNS/SnS2 microblocks serve as pillars to assemble into a 3D porous and interconnected framework, enabling fast electron/ion transport; while the GNS bridges the GNS/SnS2 microblocks into a flexible framework to provide satisfactorily mech. strength and long-range cond.  Moreover, the SnS2 nanocrystals, which chem. bond with GNS, provide sufficient active sites for Na storage and ensure the cycling stability.  Consequently, this flexible 3D-GNS/SnS2 film exhibits excellent Na-storage performances, esp. in terms of high areal capacity (2.45 mAh cm-2) and high rates with superior stability (385 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 over 1000 cycles with ≈100% retention).  A flexible SIB full cell using this anode exhibits high and stable performance under various bending situations.  Thus, this work provide a feasible route to prep. flexible electrodes with high practical viability for not only SIBs but also other energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr2h2aEibZNJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHAcHioOPm4g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXpvFahsbw%253D&amp;md5=b79bf1a76101256ff85f809a573f8e44</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201908445"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sarkar, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Q.-A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in Advanced Organic Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Synthesis, Mechanisms, Challenges and Perspectives</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered attractive alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for next-generation sustainable and large-scale electrochem. energy storage.  Org. sodium-ion batteries (OSIBs) using environmentally benign org. materials as electrodes, which demonstrate high energy/power d. and good structural designability, have recently attracted great attention.  Nevertheless, the practical applications and popularization of OSIBs are generally restricted by the intrinsic disadvantages related to org. electrodes, such as their low cond., poor stability, and high soly. in electrolytes.  Here, the latest research progress with regard to electrode materials of OSIBs, ranging from small mols. to org. polymers, is systematically reviewed, with the main focus on the mol. structure design/modification, the electrochem. behavior, and the corresponding charge-storage mechanism.  Particularly, the challenges faced by OSIBs and the effective design strategies are comprehensively summarized from three aspects: function-oriented mol. design, micromorphol. regulation, and construction of org.-inorg. composites.  Finally, the perspectives and opportunities in the research of org. electrode materials are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxZtUKbEdsT7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHAcHioOPm4g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1Grtrw%253D&amp;md5=e8f2c8e2e5398d80860a7d9330a42440</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202001440"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fast Rate and Long Life Potassium-Ion Based Dual-Ion Battery through 3D Porous Organic Negative Electrode</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-based dual ion batteries (K-DIBs) with potassium cation (K+) intercalation graphitic anodes have been investigated for their potential in large-scale energy storage applications owing to their merits of low cost and environmental friendly.  Nonetheless, graphite anodes are plagued by vol. expansion from the large K+ ions and the co-intercalation of solvent mols. during the charging.  Accordingly, org. materials stand out for the flexible adjustable structures and abundant active sites, which can accommodate cations by multiple functional groups without structural collapse.  However, K-DIBs based on org. anodes have rarely been investigated.  Herein, 3D porous dipotassium terephthalate nanosheets are synthesized via a freeze-dry method as the K-DIB anode, which can reversibly store K+ ions at a fast rate with a high specific capacity and robust stability due to the sufficient redox active sites and diffusion pathways of K+ ions in the 3D porous structure.  Consequently, a novel K-DIB configuration combining this fast kinetics org. anode and environmental friendly expanded graphite (EG) cathode is constructed (pK2TP//EG), which exhibits a high specific capacity (68 mAh g-1 at 2 C), good rate performance up to 20 C, and long cycling life with a capacity retention ~ 100% after 2000 cycles, which is the best performance obsd. among reported K-DIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIqQuN6IjGOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgrEYhl7JOuwA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXosF2qsbk%253D&amp;md5=34e7c5e58e6f6485b21d83faea6b33b5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1002/admi.201700059"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Khan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Senthilkumar, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shanker, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ko, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Redox-Additive-Enhanced High Capacitance Supercapacitors Based on Co<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> Nanosheets</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In virtue of the abundant sodium resources, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered to be one of the promising alternatives to lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, current research concs. mostly on sodium ion half-cells, and the development of sodium ion full cells with high performance remains a crit. challenge.  Here we rationally designed a full sodium-ion battery based on nanostructured Na2Ti3O7 and VOPO4 materials as the anodes and cathodes, owing to their advantageous electrochem. features.  The full cell outputs one of the highest operating voltages close to 2.9 V and delivers a large reversible capacity of 114 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.1C.  It also shows outstanding rate capability (∼74 mA h g-1 at 2C rate) and excellent cycling stability (92.4% capacity retention after 100 cycles). The structure of I (M = Fe) was solved and refined to a final R = 0.037 for 577 independent reflections.  It consists of (FeP2O7)4PO4 units interconnected so as to form a 3-dimensional framework into which the Na ions are inserted.  The units are made of a PO4 tetrahedron linked to 4 FeO6 octahedra; each octahedron is connected to a P2O7 group by 2 O atoms.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable aq. Zn/MnO2 batteries are very attractive large-scale energy storage technologies, but still suffer from limited cycle life and low capacity.  Here the novel adoption of a near-neutral acetate-based electrolyte (pH ≈ 6) is presented to promote the two-electron Mn4+/Mn2+ redox reaction and simultaneously enable a stable Zn anode.
